Middleware Stack Construction and Execution\\n\\n## Overview\\n\\nDjango's middleware system implements a sophisticated request/response processing pipeline using an \\\"onion\\\" architecture. The middleware stack is constructed once at server startup and remains immutable throughout the application's lifetime.\\n\\n## Middleware Stack Construction (django/core/handlers/base.py:27-104)\\n\\nThe `BaseHandler.load_middleware()` method (lines 27-104 in django/core/handlers/base.py) orchestrates the middleware stack construction:\\n\\n1. **Reverse Iteration**: Settings.MIDDLEWARE is processed in REVERSE order (line 41: `for middleware_path in reversed(settings.MIDDLEWARE)`). This is critical to understand.\\n\\n2. **Middleware Wrapping Pattern**: Each middleware is instantiated and wrapped around the next handler:\\n   - Line 38: `get_response = self._get_response_async if is_async else self._get_response` sets the initial handler\\n   - Line 63: `mw_instance = middleware(adapted_handler)` wraps the previous handler\\n   - Line 97: `handler = convert_exception_to_response(mw_instance)` wraps with exception handling\\n   - Line 72: `handler = adapted_handler` updates handler for next iteration\\n\\n3. **Stack Assignment**: After all middleware are chained, the complete stack is stored (line 104: `self._middleware_chain = handler`)\\n\\n## Middleware Execution Flow\\n\\n### Request Phase (Top-Down)\\nWhen a request arrives (django/core/handlers/wsgi.py:120 or django/core/handlers/asgi.py:155-167):\\n\\n1. `WSGIHandler.__call__` or `ASGIHandler.__call__` creates the request object\\n2. Calls `self.get_response(request)` (django/core/handlers/base.py:138-152)\\n3. This invokes `self._middleware_chain(request)`, which starts at the outermost middleware\\n4. Each middleware's `__call__` method (MiddlewareMixin in django/utils/deprecation.py:303-313) executes:\\n   - Calls `process_request(request)` if defined (line 309)\\n   - Returns early if a response is returned (short-circuit)\\n   - Otherwise calls `self.get_response(request)` to pass to the next layer (line 310)\\n5. The innermost middleware calls `_get_response()` which:\\n   - Applies view middleware (process_view)\\n   - Calls the actual view function\\n   - Applies template response middleware (process_template_response) if needed\\n\\n### Response Phase (Bottom-Up)\\nAfter the view executes:\\n\\n1. If short-circuited (a middleware returned a response), it goes back through ONLY the middleware layers it came in through\\n2. Otherwise, responses pass through middleware in REVERSE order of declaration\\n3. Each middleware's `process_response()` is called on the response (MiddlewareMixin:311-312)\\n4. The response bubbles back up the middleware stack\\n\\n## Exception Handling Integration\\n\\nEach middleware is wrapped with `convert_exception_to_response()` (django/core/handlers/exception.py:25-61):\\n\\n1. This wrapper converts any exception into an HttpResponse\\n2. Ensures each middleware layer gets a response (not an exception) from `get_response()`\\n3. Allows exception middleware `process_exception()` to intercept errors from deeper layers\\n4. Exceptions are processed in reverse order during the response phase (like process_response)\\n\\n## Async/Sync Adaptation\\n\\nDjango supports both sync and async middleware with automatic adaptation (django/core/handlers/base.py:106-136):\\n\\n1. Each middleware declares `sync_capable` and `async_capable` attributes\\n2. The `adapt_method_mode()` method wraps middleware to match the execution context\\n3. Sync middleware are wrapped with `sync_to_async()` when running in async context\\n4. Async middleware are wrapped with `async_to_sync()` when running in sync context\\n5. MiddlewareMixin provides both `__call__` (sync) and `__acall__` (async) methods\\n\\n## Comparison with WSGI Middleware\\n\\nWhile WSGI middleware stacks handlers by nesting callable wrappers (similar to Django's approach), Django's middleware differs in key ways:\\n\\n1. **Onion Architecture**: Django explicitly models requests/responses going \\\"in\\\" and \\\"out\\\" through the same layers, while WSGI is purely functional nesting\\n\\n2. **Special Hooks**: Django provides `process_view()`, `process_template_response()`, and `process_exception()` which have specific execution points within the request/response cycle, beyond just the basic request/response pair\\n\\n3. **Short-Circuiting**: Django's onion ensures responses bypass inner middleware they didn't see the request for, while traditional WSGI would still call all wrapper layers\\n\\n4. **Exception Handling**: Django wraps each middleware with exception handling to ensure every middleware receives an HttpResponse, not an exception. WSGI doesn't provide this integration\\n\\n5. **Settings-Driven**: Django's middleware is loaded from settings.MIDDLEWARE at startup, while WSGI applications manually nest middleware\\n\\n## Key Files Summary\\n\\n- **django/core/handlers/base.py**: Core handler containing `load_middleware()` for stack construction and `_get_response()`/`_get_response_async()` for the innermost view execution\\n- **django/core/handlers/wsgi.py**: WSGI entry point (WSGIHandler) that calls `load_middleware()` in `__init__` and handles WSGI environ\\n- **django/core/handlers/asgi.py**: ASGI entry point (ASGIHandler) that calls `load_middleware(is_async=True)` for async support\\n- **django/utils/deprecation.py**: `MiddlewareMixin` class providing the standard middleware interface with `__call__()` and `__acall__()` methods\\n- **django/core/handlers/exception.py**: `convert_exception_to_response()` wrapper ensuring exceptions are converted to responses at each middleware boundary\\n- **docs/topics/http/middleware.txt**: Official documentation explaining the onion model and middleware lifecycle\\n\"\n    98→}\n    99→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
